A lower ΔEv generally indicates higher catalytic activity, as it facilitates the creation of oxygen vacancies and thus promotes the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism. The oxidizing ability of the surface is also influenced by ΔEv, as a lower energy requirement for vacancy formation suggests that lattice oxygen is more readily available for oxidation reactions.\n\nThe study demonstrates that doping TiO2 with Fe significantly reduces the oxygen vacancy formation energy, especially at the surface. This reduction in ΔEv explains the enhanced catalytic activity observed in Fe-doped TiO2 systems, particularly for CO oxidation reactions. The presence of Fe introduces changes in the electronic structure of the oxide, which contributes to the lowering of the vacancy formation energy without significantly altering the atomic structure of anatase TiO2.\n\nThese findings highlight the importance of ΔEv as a key parameter in understanding and predicting the catalytic performance of oxide materials in oxidation reactions. By manipulating the oxygen vacancy formation energy through strategies such as doping, researchers can design more efficient catalysts for various oxidation processes.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机制在氧化物催化的氧化反应中涉及到催化剂晶格氧的参与。在这个机制中，晶格氧与底物反应形成氧化产物，同时在催化剂中产生氧空位。这个空位随后被气相氧填充，完成催化循环。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）对于决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力至关重要。较低的ΔEv通常表示更高的催化活性，因为它促进了氧空位的形成，从而促进了Mars-van Krevelen机制。表面的氧化能力也受ΔEv的影响，因为空位形成的能量需求较低意味着晶格氧更容易参与氧化反应。\n\n研究表明，用Fe掺杂TiO2显著降低了氧空位形成能，尤其是在表面。ΔEv的这种降低解释了Fe掺杂TiO2系统中观察到的增强的催化活性，特别是对于CO氧化反应。Fe的存在引入了氧化物电子结构的变化，这有助于降低空位形成能，同时不显著改变锐钛矿TiO2的原子结构。\n\n这些发现强调了ΔEv作为理解和预测氧化物材料在氧化反应中催化性能的关键参数的重要性。通过诸如掺杂等策略来操纵氧空位形成能，研究人员可以为各种氧化过程设计更高效的催化剂。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp911851h"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Many oxides catalyze oxidation reactions through the Marsvan Krevelen mechanism in which the oxygen is supplied from the surface of the oxide. The reduced oxide is reoxidized by reacting with the oxygen molecules in the gas.\"\n\n          [2] \"As the oxygen supplied to the molecule being oxidized comes from the surface of the oxide, the energy of formation of an oxygen vacancy (VO) at the surface of the oxide is often a good indicator of the oxidizing power of the oxide.\"\n\n          [3] \"Since the ease of forming oxygen vacancies is a measure of the oxidative power of the oxide in the MarsVan Krevelen mechanism, doping the ZnO surface with Au, or Ag, or Cu should increase the oxidative power and Al and Ga should decrease it.\"\n\n          [4] \"To be a good oxidation catalyst the oxide must be able to react with gaseous oxygen and recover the oxygen it has donated during the oxidation reaction. If this step is very slow the oxide will be a poor catalyst.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates as follows:\n\n          1. Oxygen for the oxidation reaction is supplied from the surface of the oxide catalyst.\n          2. This creates an oxygen vacancy on the oxide surface.\n          3. The reduced oxide is then reoxidized by reacting with oxygen molecules from the gas phase.\n\n          The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both the catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface:\n\n          1. ΔEv serves as a good indicator of the oxide's oxidizing power. A lower ΔEv generally indicates a higher oxidizing ability.\n          2. The ease of forming oxygen vacancies (lower ΔEv) is a measure of the oxidative power of the oxide in the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism.\n          3. Doping can affect ΔEv and thus the oxidative power of the oxide. For example, doping ZnO with Au, Ag, or Cu decreases ΔEv, increasing its oxidative power, while doping with Al or Ga increases ΔEv, decreasing its oxidative power.\n\n          However, it's important to note that a low ΔEv alone does not guarantee good catalytic performance. The oxide must also be able to efficiently reoxidize (i.e., react with gaseous oxygen to refill the vacancies) to complete the catalytic cycle. If this step is too slow, the oxide may be a poor catalyst despite having a low ΔEv. Therefore, while a lower ΔEv generally indicates higher oxidizing ability, the overall catalytic activity depends on the balance between the ease of oxygen vacancy formation and the ability to replenish these vacancies from the gas phase.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机制在氧化物催化的氧化反应中的运作如下：\n\n          1. 氧化反应所需的氧直接来自氧化物催化剂的表面。\n          2. 这在氧化物表面创造了一个氧空位。\n          3. 然后，还原的氧化物通过与气相中的氧分子反应而重新氧化。\n\n          氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）在决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力方面具有重要意义，原因如下：\n\n          1. ΔEv作为氧化物氧化能力的良好指标。较低的ΔEv通常表示更强的氧化能力。\n          2. 形成氧空位的容易程度（较低的ΔEv）是Mars-van Krevelen机制中氧化物氧化能力的衡量标准。\n          3. 可以通过掺杂来操纵ΔEv，从而影响氧化物的氧化能力。例如，用Au、Ag或Cu掺杂ZnO会降低ΔEv，增加氧化能力，而用Al或Ga掺杂会增加ΔEv，降低氧化能力。\n\n          然而，需要注意的是，仅仅低ΔEv并不能保证良好的催化性能。氧化物还必须能够有效地重新氧化（即与气态氧反应以填补空位）以完成催化循环。如果这一步骤太慢，尽管ΔEv低，氧化物可能是一种不好的催化剂。因此，虽然较低的ΔEv通常表示较高的氧化能力，但整体催化活性取决于氧空位形成的容易程度与从气相补充这些空位的能力之间的平衡。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp073424"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"Oxides are used as catalysts for many oxidation or oxidative dehydrogenation reactions. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Ceria can oxidise a molecule, by losing oxygen atoms with reduction of the surface. In this mechanism, the catalyst surface is reduced as it provides oxygen to oxidize the reactant molecule, and is then re-oxidized by gas-phase oxygen. \n\nFor ceria specifically, its oxygen storage capability (OSC) allows it to oxidize or reduce molecules depending on the reaction conditions. {"Quotes": "[1] \"We assume that in many systems the presence of a well-chosen dopant weakens the bond of the neighboring oxygen atoms to the surface and increases their chemical activity. Therefore, such a doped oxide is a better oxidant than the undoped one, and it is more likely to engage in an oxidation reaction by a Mars–van Krevelen mechanism in which a surface oxygen atom oxidizes a reagent and is removed from the surface leaving behind an oxygen vacancy.\"\n\n[2] \"The formation and the annihilation of the oxygen vacancies are critical steps in this Mars–van Krevelen mechanism, and this suggests that the energy of vacancy formation (ΔEv) might be a good descriptor of the catalytic properties of doped oxides.\"\n\n[3] \"We find that all the dopants studied here lower the energy of vacancy formation; therefore, the doped oxides are better oxidants than the undoped ones.\"\n\n[4] \"The energy of CO reaction with an oxygen atom from the surface layer decays linearly with the energy of vacancy formation ΔEv, whereas the energy of adsorption of O2 at a vacancy is a linear function of ΔEv. These are the only two reactions in the mechanism whose energy varies from one doped oxide to another. Because they both depend on the energy of oxygen vacancy formation, the latter quantity is a good descriptor of catalytic activity.\"\n\n[5] \"Qualitatively, a plot of activity versus ΔEv2 will be a volcano curve.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates as follows:\n\n1. A surface oxygen atom oxidizes a reactant (e.g., CO).\n2. The oxygen atom is removed from the surface, leaving behind an oxygen vacancy.\n3. The vacancy is then filled by oxygen from the gas phase, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface for several reasons:\n\n1. Descriptor of catalytic activity: ΔEv serves as a good descriptor of catalytic properties. The energies of two key reactions in the mechanism (CO reaction with surface oxygen and O2 adsorption at the vacancy) vary linearly with ΔEv.\n\n2. Oxidizing power: Lower ΔEv values indicate that the oxide is a better oxidant, as it is easier to remove oxygen atoms from the surface to participate in the oxidation reaction.\n\n3. Effect of dopants: Dopants that lower ΔEv make the doped oxides better oxidants than the undoped ones. They weaken the bond of neighboring oxygen atoms to the surface and increase their chemical activity.\n\n4. Volcano relationship: The relationship between ΔEv and catalytic activity is not simply linear. A plot of activity versus ΔEv2 is expected to show a volcano curve, indicating an optimal range for ΔEv where catalytic activity is maximized.\n\n5. {"Quotes": "[1] \"Ceria is one of the most interesting oxides industrially because it can readily create oxygen vacancies and whereby Ce4+ ions are reduced to Ce3+. This property gives ceria its high oxygen storage capacity as well as its catalytic properties;\"\n\n[2] \"Knowing the local structure, clustering properties and mobility of the oxygen vacancies on surfaces of ceria is of paramount importance for understanding their catalytic roles, both in the context of supported noble metals and in relation to the oxygen storage capacity of ceria.\"\n\n[3] \"Daturi et al. [10] found that the deNOx activity (i.e. the ability to remove nitrogen oxides, NOx, namely NO2, NO, N2O) of oxide-based catalysts such as ceria can be correlated to the concentration of surface oxygen vacancies present at the surface.\"\n\n[4] \"Daturi et al. [10] proposed a mechanism for the dissociation of NO on CeO2 surfaces, where the two oxygen atoms of two NO molecules fill two neighboring oxygen vacancies, thus acting as reoxidizing agents on the prereduced surface, while the nitrogen atoms combine to give rise to a N2 molecule.\"\n\n[5] \"The formation energy (ΔEv) for a single surface oxygen vacancy calculated using Eq. (2) is 2.10 eV\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the participation of lattice oxygen atoms from the oxide catalyst. Oxygen vacancies play a crucial role in this mechanism, and the energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface.\n\nFor ceria specifically, its ability to readily create oxygen vacancies, where Ce4+ ions are reduced to Ce3+, gives it high oxygen storage capacity and catalytic properties. The local structure, clustering properties, and mobility of these oxygen vacancies on ceria surfaces are crucial for understanding its catalytic roles.\n\nThe ΔEv influences several aspects of the catalyst's performance:\n\n1. Catalytic activity: A lower ΔEv generally indicates higher catalytic activity, as it allows for easier formation and healing of oxygen vacancies.\n\n2. Oxidizing ability: The ΔEv relates to the oxide's oxidizing power. A higher ΔEv suggests stronger metal-oxygen bonds, which can translate to stronger oxidizing ability but may reduce the ease of vacancy formation.\n\n3. Oxygen storage capacity: For ceria, its high oxygen storage capacity is directly related to its ability to form and heal oxygen vacancies.\n\n4. Reaction mechanisms: The ΔEv affects the likelihood of certain reaction pathways. For example, in NO dissociation on ceria, two NO molecules fill two neighboring oxygen vacancies, with oxygen atoms acting as reoxidizing agents and nitrogen atoms combining to form N2.\n\n5. Surface reactivity: The ease of vacancy formation, determined by ΔEv, affects the overall reactivity of the oxide surface towards various adsorbates and reactants.\n\nThe concentration of surface oxygen vacancies correlates with the deNOx activity of oxide-based catalysts like ceria. {"Quotes": "\"We use the energy of making oxygen vacancies as an indicator of the ability of the material to act as an oxidant. This vacancy is then refilled by oxygen from the gas phase, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. {"Quotes": "\"An essential step in the Mars–van Krevelen oxidation mechanism is the reaction of a surface oxygen atom with a gas-phase reducing agent, to form an oxidation product and an oxygen vacancy on the surface. The high energy required for forming an oxygen vacancy is one reason why oxides perform oxidation reactions at high temperature.\"\n\n\"We expect that the dopant lowers the oxidation temperature by weakening the bond between the oxygen and the oxide. Thus, we can measure the oxidizing capacity of an oxide by calculating the energy needed to form a vacancy.\"\n\n\"However, it is important to keep in mind that this is not a measure of catalytic activity, because a second important step is the ability to heal the vacancy formed by the oxidation process by adsorbing and activating oxygen from the gas phase.\"\n\n\"We find that doped oxides catalyze oxidation through a Mars–van Krevelen mechanism. The dopant weakens the bond between the oxide and the oxygen atoms at its surface, making them more reactive. In an oxidation reaction, the compound being oxidized takes an oxygen atom from the surface and creates an oxygen vacancy. Gas-phase O2 adsorbs on the vacancy and is activated by the electron-rich environment that it finds there. One atom in this activated O2 oxidizes a gas-phase molecule, and the other heals the oxygen vacancy in the surface.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates through a cycle of oxygen removal from the oxide surface and subsequent vacancy healing. The process involves two key steps:\n\n1. A surface oxygen atom reacts with a gas-phase reducing agent, forming an oxidation product and creating an oxygen vacancy on the surface.\n2. The oxygen vacancy is then healed by adsorbing and activating oxygen from the gas phase.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface:\n\n1. Oxidizing ability: A lower ΔEv indicates that the bond between oxygen and the oxide surface is weaker, making it easier for surface oxygen to participate in oxidation reactions. This can be used as a measure of the oxide's oxidizing capacity.\n\n2. Catalytic activity: While a lower ΔEv generally enhances the oxide's ability to oxidize gas-phase reactants, it does not directly correlate with overall catalytic activity. This is because the catalyst must also be able to efficiently heal the vacancy by adsorbing and activating gas-phase oxygen.\n\n3. Temperature dependence: The high energy typically required for oxygen vacancy formation is one reason why oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions often occur at high temperatures. Lowering ΔEv, for example through doping, can potentially reduce the temperature at which these reactions take place.\n\n4. Balancing act: An effective oxide catalyst must strike a balance between having a low enough ΔEv to allow for facile oxidation of gas-phase reactants, but not so low that it hinders the healing of oxygen vacancies by gas-phase oxygen.\n\nIn summary, while ΔEv is a crucial factor in determining an oxide's oxidizing ability, its relationship with overall catalytic activity is more complex and depends on the balance between vacancy formation and healing processes.", "Chinese": "在氧化物催化的氧化反应中，Mars-van Krevelen机理通过氧从氧化物表面移除和随后的空位愈合的循环过程来运作。该过程涉及两个关键步骤：\n\n1. 表面氧原子与气相还原剂反应，形成氧化产物并在表面创造氧空位。\n2. 然后，这个氧空位通过吸附和活化气相氧来修复。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）在决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力方面具有重要意义：\n\n1. 氧化能力：较低的ΔEv表明氧与氧化物表面之间的键合较弱，使表面氧更容易参与氧化反应。这可以用作衡量氧化物氧化能力的指标。\n\n2. 催化活性：虽然较低的ΔEv通常会增强氧化物氧化气相反应物的能力，但它与整体催化活性并不直接相关。这是因为催化剂还必须能够通过吸附和活化气相氧有效地修复空位。\n\n3. 温度依赖性：氧空位形成通常需要高能量，这是氧化物催化氧化反应常常在高温下进行的原因之一。降低ΔEv，例如通过掺杂，可能会降低这些反应发生的温度。\n\n4. 平衡作用：有效的氧化物催化剂必须在ΔEv足够低以允许气相反应物容易氧化，但又不至于低到阻碍气相氧修复氧空位之间取得平衡。\n\n总之，虽然ΔEv是决定氧化物氧化能力的关键因素，但它与整体催化活性的关系更为复杂，取决于空位形成和修复过程之间的平衡。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2006.10.009"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"The Mars–van Krevelen mechanism in which the oxygen atom responsible for the oxidation of the reactant originates from the oxide's surface.\"\n\n[2] \"The energy of oxygen-vacancy formation can be used as a crude predictor of the ability of the oxygen atoms at the surface of the oxide to engage in chemical reactions.\"\n\n[3] \"If the oxidation reaction uses oxygen from the surface, the oxidation creates oxygen vacancies on the surface. However, because oxygen is present in the gas, the vacancies will be filled by a competing process.\"\n\n[4] \"A good dopant should activate the surface oxygen but not by too much.\"\n\n[5] \"If the oxidation mechanism is Mars–van Krevelen, the oxygen atom used to oxidize the substrate must be replaced by oxygen from the gas phase; if the oxygen is too easy to remove from the surface, it should be hard to put it back.\"\n\n[6] \"An example is alkane activation in which the breaking of the C–H bond results in binding of the H atom and the alkyl to two oxygen atoms on the surface of the oxide.\"\n\n[7] \"Both mechanisms can be made more efficient by surface modifications that increase the chemical activity of the oxygen atoms in the surface.\"\n\n[8] \"If a surface modification makes the oxide a very strong oxidant (e.g., by making the energy of vacancy formation very small), this will not make it a good oxidation catalyst because the reaction will reduce the oxide and oxygen from the gas phase will not be efficient in reoxidizing it.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the oxygen atom from the oxide surface participating directly in the oxidation of the reactant. The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface for several reasons:\n\n1. ΔEv serves as an indicator of the chemical activity of surface oxygen atoms. A lower ΔEv generally suggests that oxygen atoms are more reactive and can more easily participate in oxidation reactions.\n\n2. Surface modifications that lower ΔEv can increase the efficiency of both the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism and dissociative adsorption processes, potentially improving catalytic performance.\n\n3. However, there is an optimal range for ΔEv. If it becomes too low, making the oxide a very strong oxidant, it can actually reduce catalytic effectiveness. This is because the surface may become too easily reduced, and subsequent reoxidation by gas-phase oxygen may be inefficient.\n\n4. The steady-state concentration of oxygen vacancies on the surface is determined by the competition between reduction (by the reactant) and oxidation (by gas-phase oxygen) processes.\n\n5. An example of this mechanism is seen in alkane activation, where the breaking of the C–H bond results in binding of the H atom and the alkyl to two oxygen atoms on the surface of the oxide.\n\nTherefore, while a lower ΔEv can enhance the oxidizing ability of the surface, there is a \"moderation principle\" at play. The ideal catalyst should activate surface oxygen enough to facilitate the reaction, but not so much that it becomes irreversibly reduced under reaction conditions. This highlights the importance of careful tuning of surface properties, often through doping or other modifications, to achieve optimal catalytic performance in oxidation reactions.", "Chinese": "在氧化物催化的氧化反应中，Mars-van Krevelen机制涉及氧化物表面的氧原子直接参与反应物的氧化。氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）在决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力方面具有重要意义，原因如下：\n\n1. {"Quotes": "\"If a Mars-van Krevelen mechanism is accepted for CO oxidation on Au/CeO2, then CO2 is formed when CO takes a oxygen atom from the oxide surface creating a oxygen vacancy defect, and therefore the oxidation activity of a catalyst should be inversely related to the oxygen vacancy energy formation.\"\n\n\"The energy necessary to create a oxygen vacancy defect Ef has been calculated as:\nEf = E(MTi35O71) + (1/2)E(O2) E(MTi35O72)\"\n\n\"As previously reported for ceria and rutile, doping of TiO2 anatase with Au or Fe weakens the metal-oxygen bonds around the dopant, decreases the energy necessary to form an oxygen vacancy defect from 2.7 eV in TiO2 to 1.24 eV in the Fe-doped system, and makes the reduction process exothermic in the case of Au-doped TiO2.\"\n\n\"Since the energy changes involved in the creation of the vacancy and in the subsequent O2 adsorption and vacancy healing are not as large as those found in undoped anatase, an enhanced oxidation activity can be expected in Fe-doped TiO2.\"\n\n\"Doping with Fe decreases the Ef value in 1.5 eV, suggesting that the concentration of active vacancy defects might be much higher on the Fe-doped system.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates through the following steps:\n\n1. {"Quotes": "\"This is oxygen that is active in oxidation reactions via the Mars–van Krevelen mechanism.\"\n          \n          \"The Mars–van Krevelen mechanism. This is the ability of ceria to store and release oxygen depending on the reaction conditions, i.e. under oxygen poor conditions, oxygen is released and under oxygen rich conditions, oxygen is taken up, leading to reoxidation of ceria.\"\n          \n          \"For the example of CO oxidation, it is now understood that enhancing oxygen vacancy formation is important—if this formation energy can be made smaller, then the oxidative power of ceria will be improved\"\n          \n          \"We compute the formation energy of this oxygen vacancy from\n          E (2O vac) = E (MCeO2−y) − {E (MCeO2−x) + 1/2E (O2)}, (2)\"\n          \n          \"The formation energy of the most stable active oxygen vacancy is substantially reduced compared to the corresponding undoped surface.\"\n          \n          \"For both dopants, the most stable active oxygen vacancy site is an oxygen on the surface that is not coordinated to the dopant, i.e. site I in both surfaces shown in Fig. 8. In this mechanism, a surface oxygen atom is removed to oxidize the reactant, creating an oxygen vacancy. This vacancy is then replenished by gas-phase oxygen, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\n          The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. A lower ΔEv indicates that it is easier to remove oxygen atoms from the surface, which generally leads to higher catalytic activity for oxidation reactions. This is because the removal of oxygen is often the rate-limiting step in such reactions.\n\n          The significance of ΔEv is demonstrated in the study, where doping with Pd and Ni substantially reduced the formation energy of the most stable active oxygen vacancy compared to the undoped surface. For example, Pd doping reduced the formation energy to 1.32 eV on the (111) surface and 1.36 eV on the (110) surface. A surface with a lower oxygen vacancy formation energy can more easily release oxygen, potentially making it a stronger oxidizing agent. Zr4+比Ce4+尺寸更小，这为Ce3+的形成释放了应力\n          2. 较小的还原能\n          3. 与纯氧化铈相比，具有更高的氧移动性\n\n          总之，在Mars-van Krevelen机制的背景下，较低的Evac通常与氧化物表面更高的催化活性和氧化能力相关。这个参数有助于理解和预测不同氧化物催化剂在氧化反应中的相对活性。", "Doi": "10.1007/s10562-010-0446-5"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"In this mechanism, the reductant is oxidized by the oxygen atoms from the surface of the oxide (not by adsorbed oxygen). The easier it is to make a vacancy, the better oxidant the surface is.\"\n\n          [2] \"This implies that doping an oxide surface with a LVD makes it a better oxidant. This is not to say that the best oxidant is the best oxidation catalyst. In the MvK mechanism, the gas-phase oxygen reoxidizes the surface reduced by the reactant (e.g., CO or CH4).\"\n\n          [3] \"If the oxygen is too easy to remove, it is difficult to put it back. In designing an oxidation catalyst, by doping an oxide, one should aim for the middle ground: the dopant should make it easy to remove an oxygen atom, but not too easy. We call this a moderation principle.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen (MvK) mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates through the following steps:\n\n          1. The reductant is oxidized by oxygen atoms from the oxide surface, not by adsorbed oxygen.\n          2. This process creates oxygen vacancies on the surface.\n          3. Gas-phase oxygen then reoxidizes the reduced surface, filling the vacancies.\n\n          The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface:\n\n          1. Lower ΔEv makes the surface a better oxidant, as it's easier to remove oxygen atoms for the oxidation reaction.\n          2. However, the best oxidant is not necessarily the best catalyst. There needs to be a balance:\n             - If ΔEv is too low, it becomes difficult to reoxidize the surface with gas-phase oxygen.\n             - If ΔEv is too high, the surface won't readily give up oxygen for the oxidation reaction.\n          3. The ideal catalyst follows a \"moderation principle\": ΔEv should be low enough to allow easy removal of oxygen atoms, but not so low that reoxidation becomes difficult.\n          4. Doping the oxide surface with low-valence dopants (LVDs) can lower ΔEv, potentially improving its catalytic activity, but care must be taken to maintain the right balance for optimal performance.\n\n          In summary, while a lower ΔEv generally indicates a better oxidizing ability of the oxide surface, the optimal catalytic activity is achieved with a moderate ΔEv that balances the ease of oxygen removal and replenishment in the MvK mechanism.", "Chinese": "在氧化物催化的氧化反应中，Mars-van Krevelen（MvK）机理通过以下步骤运作：\n\n          1. 还原剂被氧化物表面的氧原子氧化，而不是被吸附的氧气氧化。\n          2. 这个过程在表面创造了氧空位。\n          3. 气相氧然后重新氧化还原后的表面，填补空位。\n\n          氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）对于决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力至关重要：\n\n          1. 较低的ΔEv使表面成为更好的氧化剂，因为更容易移除氧原子进行氧化反应。\n          2. 然而，最好的氧化剂不一定是最好的催化剂。需要保持平衡：\n             - 如果ΔEv太低，用气相氧重新氧化表面变得困难。\n             - 如果ΔEv太高，表面不会轻易释放氧进行氧化反应。\n          3. 理想的催化剂遵循\"适度原则\"：ΔEv应该足够低以允许容易移除氧原子，但不能低到使重新氧化变得困难。\n          4. 用低价掺杂剂（LVDs）掺杂氧化物表面可以降低ΔEv，潜在地提高其催化活性，但必须注意保持适当的平衡以获得最佳性能。\n\n          总之，虽然较低的ΔEv通常表示氧化物表面具有更好的氧化能力，但最佳的催化活性是通过在MvK机制中平衡氧的去除和补充容易程度的适度ΔEv来实现的。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp301341"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"We show that doping with Au, Ag, Cu, Pt, Pd, Ni reduces dramatically the bond of surface oxygen to titania or ceria, making them better oxidation catalysts.\"\n\n[2] \"To determine to what extent the oxide becomes a better oxidant when doped with Au, we have calculated the energy (Evf) required for removing one of the oxygen atoms to form a vacancy in the surface layer and half an oxygen molecule in the gas phase.\"\n\n[3] \"While CO adsorption and CO2 desorption produce the desired product, this reactions is not catalytic because it removes irreversibly oxygen from the surface. To have a catalyst we must find how gas-phase oxygen fills the oxygen vacancies formed by CO2 desorption.\"\n\n[4] \"After adsorption, the oxygen molecule reacts with gas-phase CO to form a carbonate (figure 1e), with a very substantial release of energy (about 4 eV). This complex decomposes to release CO2 and leaves behind an oxygen atom that fills the vacancy. This restores the surface to its initial state, which means that this set of reactions is catalytic.\"\n\n[5] \"Doping weakens dramatically the bond of surface oxygen to the oxide, even when a Ti atom is substituted by Au in the slab sub layer (not shown).\"\n\n[6] \"Our results suggest that the Au-doped TiO2 is a stronger oxidant than the pure oxide or the one with a neutral Au cluster on it.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates through a cycle of oxygen removal from the catalyst surface and subsequent replenishment. Initially, a surface oxygen atom reacts with the molecule to be oxidized (e.g., CO), forming the oxidized product (e.g., CO2) and leaving an oxygen vacancy on the surface. Then, gas-phase oxygen fills this vacancy, restoring the catalyst to its original state.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. A lower ΔEv indicates that surface oxygen is more easily removed, making the oxide a better oxidant and potentially a more active catalyst. Doping the oxide with certain metals (like Au, Ag, Cu, Pt, Pd, Ni) can significantly reduce ΔEv, enhancing the oxide's oxidizing power and catalytic activity. This effect is due to the weakening of the bond between surface oxygen atoms and the oxide lattice in the presence of the dopant.\n\nHowever, an optimal balance is necessary. If ΔEv is too low, the oxide may become unstable or have difficulty replenishing its oxygen. Conversely, if ΔEv is too high, the oxide won't readily give up its oxygen for oxidation reactions. Therefore, ΔEv serves as a key indicator of an oxide's potential as an oxidation catalyst, with an ideal value allowing for both efficient oxidation and catalyst regeneration.", "Chinese": "在氧化物催化的氧化反应中，Mars-van Krevelen机制通过催化剂表面氧的移除和随后的补充循环来运作。首先，表面氧原子与待氧化分子（如CO）反应，形成氧化产物（如CO2），并在表面留下氧空位。然后，气相氧填补这个空位，使催化剂恢复到原始状态。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）在决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力方面起着关键作用。较低的ΔEv表明表面氧更容易被移除，使氧化物成为更好的氧化剂，可能成为更活跃的催化剂。用某些金属（如Au、Ag、Cu、Pt、Pd、Ni）掺杂氧化物可以显著降低ΔEv，增强氧化物的氧化能力和催化活性。这种效果是由于掺杂剂的存在使表面氧原子与氧化物晶格之间的键合减弱。\n\n然而，需要一个最佳平衡。如果ΔEv太低，氧化物可能变得不稳定或难以补充氧。相反，如果ΔEv太高，氧化物就不会轻易释放氧进行氧化反应。因此，ΔEv作为氧化物作为氧化催化剂潜力的关键指标，其理想值应允许高效的氧化和催化剂再生。", "Doi": "10.1007/s10562-005-0014-6"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"We characterize the reactivity of the oxygen atoms at the surface of the oxide by four quantities: the energy ΔEv to make an oxygen vacancy in the surface; the binding energies ΔEH and ΔECH3 of a H atom or a CH3 radical to a surface oxygen atom; and the energy ΔECH4 of dissociative adsorption of methane (to form a hydroxyl and a methoxy group).\"\n\n[2] \"In all examples that we have examined, the presence of an LVD in the surface of an oxide makes ΔEv much smaller and ΔEH, ΔECH3, and ΔECH4 much larger than in the case of the undoped oxide.\"\n\n[3] \"To probe the change in oxygen activity caused by the dopant, we used the energy ΔEv of making an oxygen vacancy, the energies ΔEH and ΔECH3 to bind a H atom or a CH3 radical to an oxygen atom in the surface layer, and the energy ΔECH4 of the dissociative adsorption of methane to form a hydroxyl and a methoxide.\"\n\n[4] \"On an oxide doped with an LVD, it is much easier (than on the undoped oxide) to remove an oxygen atom from the surface to form 1/2 O2 in the gas phase and an oxygen vacancy on the surface.\"\n\n[5] \"The presence of the LVD1 substantially increases the energy gained by the dissociative adsorption of methane. Assuming that the EvansPolanyi rules work for this case, this will lower the activation energy for breaking the CH bond and oxides doped with LVD1 should be better catalysts for methane activation than the undoped oxides.\"\n\n[6] \"If these two species are not removed promptly from the surface, their presence substantially lower the activity of the surface (by the chemical compensation effect) and they poison the catalyst. We may have a situation where the rate-limiting step is not the breaking of the CH bond but the removal of H and CH3 from the surface.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the participation of lattice oxygen from the oxide surface. The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) plays a crucial role in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface.\n\nA lower ΔEv indicates that it is easier to remove oxygen atoms from the oxide surface, which is essential for the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism to operate efficiently. When ΔEv is lower, the oxide surface can more readily provide lattice oxygen for the oxidation reaction, making it a more active catalyst.\n\nThe significance of ΔEv lies in its direct relationship to the oxide's ability to release and replenish oxygen during the catalytic cycle. A lower ΔEv suggests that the oxide can more easily form oxygen vacancies, which are crucial for the adsorption and activation of reactant molecules. These vacancies can then be refilled by gas-phase oxygen or other oxidizing species, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nAdditionally, other parameters (ΔEH, ΔECH3, and ΔECH4) are mentioned, which along with ΔEv, provide a comprehensive picture of the oxide surface's reactivity. These parameters indicate how strongly the surface interacts with various species involved in catalytic reactions, further influencing the overall catalytic performance.\n\nIn the context of doped oxides, particularly those with low valence dopants (LVDs), the ΔEv is typically reduced compared to undoped oxides. This suggests that doping can be a strategy to enhance the catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of oxide surfaces for reactions following the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism.\n\nHowever, it's important to note that while a lower ΔEv generally indicates higher catalytic activity, it may also lead to faster deactivation of the catalyst if the oxygen vacancies are not promptly refilled. The literature also points out a potential complication where the dissociation products of reactants (e.g., H and CH3 from methane) can act as compensating agents, potentially poisoning the catalyst if not removed promptly. This suggests that in some cases, the rate-limiting step in catalytic oxidation reactions might shift from the initial bond breaking to the removal of reaction intermediates from the surface.\n\nIn summary, ΔEv is a critical parameter in the Mars-van Krevelen mechanism, influencing both catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of oxide surfaces. {"Quotes": "[1] \"In most cases the molecule to be oxidized takes oxygen from the surface creating oxygen vacancies on it. The oxygen molecule from the gas phase annihilates the vacancies closing thus the catalytic cycle.\"\n\n[2] \"Ceria surfaces have a relatively small oxygen vacancy formation energy, which arises from the ability of ceria to change oxidation state from (formally) +4 to (formally) +3.\"\n\n[3] \"It is believed that doping facilitates the reduction of ceria [412] by weakening CeO bonds around the dopant. A number of computational studies have demonstrated that the oxygen vacancy formation energy is lower when the surface is doped with Zr [3,4,11].\"\n\n[4] \"The key finding is that upon doping of the (110) and (100) surfaces with Au, the oxygen vacancy formation energy is negative, indicating that if the system is in equilibrium, oxygen vacancies will be thermodynamically favourable.\"\n\n[5] \"A good oxidant needs to give away oxygen easily. A good oxidation catalyst must strike a balance [12]: if it gives oxygen too easily it will not be effective in taking oxygen from the gas phase.\"\n\n[6] \"Since at sufficiently high temperature and an oxygen pressure of 1 atm almost all dopants have an oxygen vacancy next to them, it is the formation of a second oxygen vacancy that determines the oxidation activity of the doped surface.\"\n\n[7] \"The vacancy formation energies show that the dopant facilitates the formation of a second oxygen vacancy on (110) but not on (100), revealing a notable surface dependence that could be exploited in the design of nanostructured ceria catalysts.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates through a cycle where:\n\n1. The molecule to be oxidized takes oxygen from the oxide surface, creating oxygen vacancies.\n2. Oxygen from the gas phase then fills these vacancies, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface because:\n\n1. A lower ΔEv indicates that oxygen can be more easily removed from the surface, potentially increasing catalytic activity.\n2. However, an optimal balance is needed - if oxygen is removed too easily, the surface may not effectively take oxygen from the gas phase to heal vacancies, potentially limiting its effectiveness as an oxidation catalyst.\n3. Ceria's effectiveness as a catalyst stems from its relatively small ΔEv, which is related to its ability to change oxidation states from Ce4+ to Ce3+.\n4. Doping, such as with Au or Zr, can further lower ΔEv by weakening metal-oxygen bonds, making oxygen removal even easier.\n5. In some cases, like Au-doped ceria (110) and (100) surfaces, ΔEv becomes negative, indicating that oxygen vacancy formation becomes thermodynamically favorable.\n6. The formation of a second oxygen vacancy, especially in doped surfaces, can be crucial in determining the oxidation activity of the catalyst.\n7. Surface structure plays a role in the effect of doping, as demonstrated by the different behaviors of (110) and (100) surfaces when doped.\n\nThus, ΔEv serves as a key indicator of a material's potential as an oxidation catalyst, with lower values generally indicating higher activity, but with the caveat that extremely low values may impair the catalyst's ability to complete the full oxidation cycle. The design of effective catalysts involves optimizing this balance, potentially through strategies such as doping and controlling surface structure.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机制在氧化物催化的氧化反应中通过以下循环运作：\n\n1. 待氧化的分子从氧化物表面获取氧，在表面形成氧空位。\n2. 气相中的氧分子随后填补这些空位，完成催化循环。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）对于决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力至关重要，因为：\n\n1. 较低的ΔEv表明氧可以更容易从表面移除，可能增加催化活性。\n2. 然而，需要一个最佳平衡 - 如果氧被移除得太容易，表面可能无法有效地从气相中获取氧来愈合空位，可能限制其作为氧化催化剂的有效性。\n3. 氧化铈作为催化剂的有效性源于其相对较小的ΔEv，这与其能够从Ce4+变为Ce3+的氧化态变化能力有关。\n4. 掺杂（如用Au或Zr）可以通过削弱金属-氧键进一步降低ΔEv，使氧的移除更加容易。\n5. 在某些情况下，如Au掺杂的氧化铈(110)和(100)表面，ΔEv变为负值，表明氧空位形成在热力学上变得有利。\n6. 第二个氧空位的形成，特别是在掺杂表面上，可能对决定催化剂的氧化活性至关重要。\n7. 表面结构在掺杂效应中起着重要作用，如(110)和(100)表面在掺杂时表现出的不同行为所示。\n\n因此，ΔEv作为材料作为氧化催化剂潜力的关键指标，较低的值通常表示较高的活性，但需要注意的是，极低的值可能会损害催化剂完成完整氧化循环的能力。设计有效的催化剂涉及优化这种平衡，可能通过掺杂和控制表面结构等策略来实现。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.susc.2008.06.028"},
{"Quotes": "\"Consequently, oxygen vacancy defects can play a central role: surface lattice oxygen may act as an oxidant for adsorbates, thus creating oxygen vacancies (i.e., Mars–van Krevelen mechanism)\"\n\n          \"We focus here on two fundamental aspects: (i) the energy required to form the oxygen defects and (ii) the electronic structure of the reduced systems\"\n\n          \"To illustrate stability of these vacancies, we list in Table I the formation energy per vacancy (Ev^a)\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism operates in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions by using surface lattice oxygen as an oxidant for adsorbates, which creates oxygen vacancies on the oxide surface. {"Quotes": "[1] \"If a doped oxide is used as an oxidation catalyst by a Marsvan Krevelen mechanism, then one should seek a dopant that makes it easy to make oxygen vacancies, but not too easy.\"\n\n[2] \"Informally, we call this a moderation principle. The point is that, if the oxygen is very easy to remove, then it is a very good oxidant, but not a good oxidation catalyst, since it is difficult to put the oxygen back.\"\n\n[3] \"We find that the ease with which one can make oxygen vacancies correlates with the reactivity of the surface toward methane dissociation.\"\n\n[4] \"The energy of oxygen-vacancy formation, ΔEv, on Cu-, Zn-, Mg-, Fe-, or Al-doped La2O3 (001) and (011) surfaces. We found that these dopants cause a very substantial lowering of ΔEv from 6.44 eV for pure La2O3(001) to 0.52, 2.01, and 2.59 eV for La2O3(001) doped with Cu, Zn, or Mg, respectively.\"\n\n[5] \"Cu-doped lanthanum oxide is an example of this. The oxygen is so easy to remove that it is likely to be lost at a temperature lower than that of methane activation. This means that, under reaction conditions, the catalyst is reduced; our calculations show that the reduced CuLa2O3 does not break the CH bond efficiently.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the removal of lattice oxygen atoms from the catalyst surface to oxidize reactants, followed by the replenishment of these oxygen vacancies by gas-phase oxygen. The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) plays a crucial role in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface.\n\nA lower ΔEv generally correlates with higher reactivity towards reactants like methane, as it is easier to remove oxygen from the surface to participate in the oxidation reaction. However, there is an optimal range for ΔEv that balances reactivity with stability, known as the \"moderation principle.\" If ΔEv is too low, the oxide becomes an excellent oxidant but a poor catalyst, as it loses oxygen too easily and struggles to replenish it from the gas phase. Conversely, if ΔEv is too high, the oxide is unreactive.\n\nThe ideal catalyst should have a moderate ΔEv, making it easy enough to create oxygen vacancies for oxidation reactions, but not so easy that the catalyst becomes rapidly reduced under reaction conditions. This balance ensures that the catalyst can effectively oxidize reactants while maintaining its ability to complete the catalytic cycle by replenishing lost oxygen.\n\nDopants can be used to tune ΔEv to achieve this balance. For example, doping La2O3 with Cu, Zn, or Mg significantly lowers ΔEv compared to the pure oxide, potentially enhancing its catalytic activity. However, the optimal dopant and doping level depend on the specific reaction conditions and desired catalytic properties. {"Quotes": "\"It is widely accepted (224, 225) that most oxidation or oxidative dehydrogenation reactions catalyzed by oxides take place through a Marsvan Krevelen (226) mechanism. In such reactions, the gases introduced in the reactor contain a reductant (e.g., an alkane, CO, H2) and an oxidant (e.g., O2, CO2, N2O). In the Marsvan Krevelen mechanism, the reductant is oxidized by the oxygen atoms from the oxides surface layer (not by adsorbed oxygen or by gas-phase oxygen). When the oxidation products desorb, they leave behind oxygen vacancies. The role of the gas-phase oxidant, introduced with the feed, is to annihilate the oxygen vacancies (to reoxidize the surface).\"\n\n          \"We assume that there is a connection between the ability of surface oxygen to act as an oxidizing agent and the energy ΔEv required for forming an oxygen vacancy. To be precise, ΔEv is the energy of the reaction where Ox is the oxide (doped or not) and Oxv is the oxide with an oxygen vacancy on the surface. The assumption is that the smaller is ΔEv, the better oxidant is the surface.\"\n\n          \"Once we accept this idea, we can calculate ΔEv for a quick screening of the oxidative power of various oxides (doped or undoped). Moreover, if we want to make an oxide a better oxidant, we should look for modifications that make ΔEv smaller. However, one must keep in mind that a very small ΔEv means that the surface is a good oxidant, but it is not necessarily a good oxidation catalyst. To complete the catalytic cycle, the gaseous oxidant (oxygen, CO2, N2O) must be able to reoxidize the surface. If oxygen is too easy to remove from the surface layer, it will be difficult to put back.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions operates as follows:\n\n1. The reductant (e.g., alkane, CO, H2) is oxidized by oxygen atoms from the oxide's surface layer, not by adsorbed or gas-phase oxygen.\n\n2. When oxidation products desorb, they leave behind oxygen vacancies on the surface.\n\n3. The gas-phase oxidant (e.g., O2, CO2, N2O) then reoxidizes the surface by filling these vacancies.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is significant in determining both catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface:\n\n1. ΔEv is assumed to be inversely related to the oxidizing power of the surface - the smaller the ΔEv, the better the oxidant.\n\n2. ΔEv can be calculated to quickly screen the oxidative power of various oxides, both doped and undoped.\n\n3. To improve an oxide's oxidizing ability, modifications that decrease ΔEv should be sought.\n\n4. However, a very small ΔEv, while indicating a good oxidant, does not necessarily mean a good oxidation catalyst. If oxygen is too easily removed from the surface, it may be difficult to reoxidize the surface and complete the catalytic cycle.\n\n5. The rate-limiting step in most cases is the reaction of the reductant with surface oxygen, not the reoxidation of the surface.\n\nThus, ΔEv serves as a crucial parameter in understanding and optimizing oxide catalysts for oxidation reactions, balancing the need for both good oxidizing ability and catalyst regeneration.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机理在氧化物催化的氧化反应中的运作如下：\n\n1. 还原剂（如烷烃、CO、H2）被氧化物表面层的氧原子氧化，而不是被吸附氧或气相氧氧化。\n\n2. 当氧化产物脱附时，它们在表面留下氧空位。\n\n3. 气相氧化剂（如O2、CO2、N2O）随后通过填充这些空位来重新氧化表面。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）在决定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力方面具有重要意义：\n\n1. ΔEv被假定与表面的氧化能力呈反比关系 - ΔEv越小，表面的氧化能力越强。\n\n2. 可以计算ΔEv来快速筛选各种氧化物（掺杂或未掺杂）的氧化能力。\n\n3. 为了提高氧化物的氧化能力，应寻求能降低ΔEv的修饰方法。\n\n4. 然而，非常小的ΔEv虽然表明是好的氧化剂，但并不一定意味着是好的氧化催化剂。如果氧气从表面太容易被移除，可能难以重新氧化表面并完成催化循环。\n\n5. 在大多数情况下，限速步骤是还原剂与表面氧的反应，而不是表面的重新氧化。\n\n因此，ΔEv作为理解和优化氧化反应的氧化物催化剂的关键参数，平衡了良好氧化能力和催化剂再生的需求。", "Doi": "10.1021/cr300418s_7"},
{"Quotes": "\"Moreover, the formation and the annihilation of oxygen vacancies are essential steps in the Marsvan Krevelen mechanism (8-10) for catalytic oxidation.\"\n\n\"When an oxygen atom is removed from the surface of rutile TiO2(110), to make an oxygen vacancy, two unpaired electrons are left in the oxide.\"\n\n\"The oxygen-vacancy formation energy (Evf) was calculated as\n\nEvf = 1/2E[O2] + E[TiO2(S)] - E[TiO2(R)]\n\nwhere E[O2] is the total energy of O2 in gas phase, E[TiO2(S)] is the total energy of the stoichiometric slab, and E[TiO2(R)] is the total energy of a relaxed, partially reduced TiO2 slab having one bridging O vacancy on the surface of the supercell.\"\n\n\"The removal of a neutral oxygen atom leaves behind two electrons that had been engaged in two TiO bonds that were broken when the vacancy was formed.\"\n\n\"Forming the vacancy reduces the two 6c-Ti* atoms from a formal charge of 4+ to a formal charge of 3+.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the formation and annihilation of oxygen vacancies on the oxide surface. In this process, an oxygen atom from the oxide lattice participates in the oxidation of the reactant, creating an oxygen vacancy. This vacancy is then refilled by oxygen from the gas phase, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv or Evf) is a crucial parameter in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. A lower vacancy formation energy generally indicates a more active catalyst, as it is easier to remove oxygen from the lattice to participate in the oxidation reaction. However, if the vacancy formation energy is too low, the oxide may become unstable or over-reduced, potentially leading to a loss of catalytic activity.\n\nThe vacancy formation energy also influences the oxidizing ability of the surface. A higher ΔEv typically corresponds to a stronger oxidizing power, as the oxide holds onto its oxygen more tightly. Conversely, a lower ΔEv may indicate a weaker oxidizing ability but potentially higher activity for certain reactions.\n\nThe formation of an oxygen vacancy leaves behind two unpaired electrons, which can localize on nearby metal cations (in this case, Ti atoms), reducing them from their formal oxidation state. For example, in TiO2, forming the vacancy reduces two Ti atoms from a formal charge of 4+ to 3+. This reduction of metal cations and the associated structural changes (such as polaron formation) can significantly affect the surface chemistry and reactivity.\n\nThe oxygen vacancy formation energy (Evf) is calculated using density functional theory, considering the energies of the gas-phase oxygen molecule, the stoichiometric oxide slab, and the reduced oxide slab with an oxygen vacancy. This calculation helps in understanding the energetics of vacancy formation and its implications for catalytic behavior.\n\nUnderstanding and controlling the oxygen vacancy formation energy is crucial for designing and optimizing oxide catalysts for specific oxidation reactions. It allows researchers to balance the trade-off between catalytic activity and oxidizing power, tailoring the catalyst properties to the desired reaction.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机理在氧化物催化的氧化反应中涉及氧化物表面氧空位的形成和消除。在这个过程中，氧化物晶格中的一个氧原子参与反应物的氧化，形成氧空位。然后，这个空位被气相中的氧重新填充，完成催化循环。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv或Evf）是决定氧化物表面催化活性和氧化能力的关键参数。较低的空位形成能通常表示催化剂更活跃，因为从晶格中移除氧以参与氧化反应更容易。然而，如果空位形成能太低，氧化物可能变得不稳定或过度还原，潜在导致催化活性的损失。\n\n空位形成能也影响表面的氧化能力。较高的ΔEv通常对应于更强的氧化能力，因为氧化物更紧密地保持其氧。相反，较低的ΔEv可能表示较弱的氧化能力，但对某些反应可能具有更高的活性。\n\n氧空位的形成会留下两个未配对电子，这些电子可以局域化在附近的金属阳离子上（在这种情况下是Ti原子），将它们从正式氧化态还原。例如，在TiO2中，形成空位将两个Ti原子从正式电荷4+还原为3+。这种金属阳离子的还原以及相关的结构变化（如极化子形成）可以显著影响表面化学和反应性。\n\n氧空位形成能（Evf）使用密度泛函理论计算，考虑气相氧分子、化学计量比氧化物板条和带有氧空位的还原氧化物板条的能量。这种计算有助于理解空位形成的能量学及其对催化行为的影响。\n\n理解和控制氧空位形成能对于设计和优化特定氧化反应的氧化物催化剂至关重要。它允许研究人员平衡催化活性和氧化能力之间的权衡，根据所需的反应调整催化剂性质。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp111209a"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"The oxygen vacancy formation energy on PdxCe1xO2(1 1 1) is less endothermic than on CeO2(1 1 1), and the methane activation barrier is lower over PdxCe1xO2(1 1 1) than over CeO2(1 1 1).\"\n\n[2] \"Water is formed by adsorption of H atoms on surface oxygen atoms followed by desorption of H2O(g) to leave a surface oxygen vacancy.\"\n\n[3] \"We use ab initio thermodynamics to evaluate the dependence of rate-determining steps and the overall reaction mechanism on catalytic operating conditions including temperature and partial pressure of reactants and products.\"\n\n[4] \"Regardless of the initial oxidation state, the oxidation state of Pd cycles between either Pd0/Pd2+ or Pd2+/Pd4+ during the full reaction turnover of methane oxidation.\"\n\n[5] \"The consideration of product formation and vacancy filling sequentially throughout the mechanism can be contrasted with the approach of Knapp et al. [18]. Knapp et al. included all water formation energies at the final step and neglected vacancy filling in their analysis of the reaction energy diagram for methane oxidation over pure CeO2(1 1 1).\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the participation of lattice oxygen atoms from the catalyst surface. In this mechanism, surface oxygen reacts with adsorbed species to form products (such as water), creating oxygen vacancies on the surface. These vacancies are then refilled by gas-phase oxygen or bulk oxygen diffusion, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\nThe energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. A lower ΔEv generally indicates higher catalytic activity, as it facilitates the participation of lattice oxygen in the reaction. This is exemplified by the PdxCe1xO2(1 1 1) surface, which has a lower oxygen vacancy formation energy compared to CeO2(1 1 1), correlating with its lower methane activation barrier and thus higher activity.\n\nThe oxidizing ability of the surface is also influenced by ΔEv. A surface with lower ΔEv can more readily provide oxygen for oxidation reactions, potentially leading to higher oxidation rates. However, if ΔEv is too low, it may result in over-oxidation of reactants or products, potentially reducing selectivity.\n\nThe significance of ΔEv extends to the overall reaction mechanism, including product formation and vacancy refilling steps. These steps are crucial for completing the catalytic cycle and maintaining the catalyst's activity over time. The sequential consideration of these steps throughout the reaction mechanism, as opposed to treating them as final steps, provides a more comprehensive understanding of the oxidation process and the role of oxygen vacancies in catalysis.\n\nIn the context of methane oxidation, the cycling of Pd oxidation states (between Pd0/Pd2+ or Pd2+/Pd4+) during the reaction turnover illustrates the dynamic nature of the catalyst surface and the importance of redox processes in the overall mechanism. This cycling, coupled with the formation and filling of oxygen vacancies, highlights the complexity of the catalytic process and the critical role of the oxide surface in facilitating the reaction.\n\nThe overall catalytic performance is influenced by the balance between vacancy formation and refilling rates, which depend on reaction conditions such as temperature and partial pressures of reactants and products. Understanding these relationships allows for the design of more effective oxide catalysts for oxidation reactions.", "Chinese": "在氧化物催化的氧化反应中，Mars-van Krevelen机理涉及催化剂表面晶格氧原子的参与。在这种机理中，表面氧与吸附物种反应形成产物（如水），在表面上创造氧空位。这些空位随后被气相氧或体相氧扩散所填充，完成催化循环。\n\n氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv）对于确定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力至关重要。较低的ΔEv通常表示更高的催化活性，因为它促进了晶格氧参与反应。PdxCe1xO2(1 1 1)表面就是一个例子，与CeO2(1 1 1)相比，它具有较低的氧空位形成能，与其较低的甲烷活化能垒相关，因此具有更高的活性。\n\n表面的氧化能力也受ΔEv的影响。ΔEv较低的表面可以更容易地为氧化反应提供氧，可能导致更高的氧化速率。然而，如果ΔEv过低，可能会导致反应物或产物的过度氧化，可能降低选择性。\n\nΔEv的重要性还延伸到整个反应机制，包括产物形成和空位填充步骤。这些步骤对于完成催化循环和维持催化剂的长期活性至关重要。在整个反应机制中sequential考虑这些步骤，而不是将它们作为最后步骤处理，可以更全面地理解氧化过程和氧空位在催化中的作用。\n\n在甲烷氧化的背景下，Pd氧化态在反应周转过程中的循环（在Pd0/Pd2+或Pd2+/Pd4+之间）说明了催化剂表面的动态性质以及氧化还原过程在整个机理中的重要性。这种循环，加上氧空位的形成和填充，突出了催化过程的复杂性以及氧化物表面在促进反应中的关键作用。\n\n整体催化性能受空位形成和填充速率平衡的影响，这些速率取决于反应条件，如温度和反应物及产物的分压。理解这些关系有助于设计更有效的氧化物催化剂用于氧化反应。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2010.11.006"},

In this mechanism, lattice oxygen oxidizes the reactant and creates an oxygen vacancy, which is then refilled by gas-phase oxygen. The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface.\n\nA lower ΔEv generally corresponds to higher catalytic activity, as it allows for easier removal of lattice oxygen to participate in the oxidation reaction. {"Quotes": "No relevant quotes provided in the answer results.", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the participation of lattice oxygen from the oxide catalyst. In this mechanism, a reactant molecule is oxidized by removing an oxygen atom from the catalyst surface, creating an oxygen vacancy. This vacancy is then refilled by gas phase oxygen, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\n          The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv) is a key parameter that influences both the catalytic activity and oxidizing ability of the oxide surface:\n\n          1. Catalytic activity: A lower ΔEv generally leads to higher catalytic activity, as it is easier to remove lattice oxygen for the oxidation reaction. However, if ΔEv is too low, the catalyst may become unstable or over-reactive.\n\n          2. Oxidizing ability: ΔEv correlates with the oxide's oxidizing power. A lower ΔEv indicates stronger oxidizing ability, as oxygen can be more readily removed from the lattice to oxidize reactants. Oxides with moderate ΔEv values tend to have optimal oxidizing ability, balancing reactivity and selectivity.\n\n          3. Selectivity: The value of ΔEv can impact reaction selectivity by influencing the strength of oxygen binding to the surface and its reactivity. An optimal intermediate ΔEv is often desired to balance activity and selectivity.\n\n          4. Oxygen mobility: A lower ΔEv typically corresponds to higher oxygen mobility within the lattice, which can enhance the catalyst's ability to transport oxygen to active sites.\n\n          5. Catalyst durability: Very low ΔEv values may lead to excessive oxygen loss and structural instability, potentially causing catalyst deactivation over time.\n\n          ΔEv serves as a descriptor for predicting and understanding catalytic behavior in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions, helping to guide the design and selection of catalysts for specific applications. Tuning the ΔEv through catalyst composition and structure is a crucial strategy for optimizing oxide catalysts for specific oxidation reactions, balancing activity, selectivity, and stability.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机理在氧化物催化的氧化反应中涉及氧化物催化剂中晶格氧的参与。在这个机理中，反应物分子通过从催化剂表面移除一个氧原子而被氧化，从而产生氧空位。然后这个空位被气相氧重新填充，完成催化循环。\n\n          氧空位形成能(ΔEv)是一个关键参数，影响氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力：\n\n          1. 催化活性：较低的ΔEv通常会导致更高的催化活性，因为更容易移除晶格氧进行氧化反应。但是，如果ΔEv太低，催化剂可能会变得不稳定或反应过度。\n\n          2. 氧化能力：ΔEv与氧化物的氧化能力相关。较低的ΔEv表示更强的氧化能力，因为氧更容易从晶格中移除以氧化反应物。具有适中ΔEv值的氧化物往往具有最佳的氧化能力，平衡反应性和选择性。\n\n          3. 选择性：ΔEv的值可能通过影响氧与表面的结合强度及其反应性来影响反应选择性。通常需要一个适中的ΔEv来平衡活性和选择性。\n\n          4. 氧移动性：较低的ΔEv通常对应于晶格内更高的氧移动性，这可以增强催化剂将氧运输到活性位点的能力。\n\n          5. 催化剂耐久性：非常低的ΔEv值可能导致过度的氧损失和结构不稳定性，可能导致催化剂随时间失活。\n\n          ΔEv作为预测和理解氧化物催化氧化反应中催化行为的描述符，有助于指导特定应用的催化剂设计和选择。通过催化剂组成和结构调整ΔEv是优化氧化物催化剂用于特定氧化反应的关键策略，平衡活性、选择性和稳定性。", "Doi": "10.1080/01614940.2011.613330"},

{"Quotes": "[1] \"The oxygen vacancy formation is described by the reaction of Ce1xMxO2  Ce1xMxO2δ + 1/2O2.\"\n          [2] \"The oxygen vacancy formation energy, Ef, was computed according to the eq 1.\"\n          [3] \"Compared to CeO2 and Ce0.875Zr0.125O2, the smaller Ef (1.03 for Ce0.875Ru0.125O2; 3.20 and 2.03 eV for CeO2 and Ce0.875Zr0.125O2) indicates that Ce0.875Ru0.125O2 shows higher OSC property than CeO2 and Ce0.875Zr0.125O2, which is consistent with the experimental results.\"\n          [4] \"The Ru dopant promotes CO oxidation without any activation energy leading to O vacancy formation and CO2 desorption. Molecular O2 adsorbs at the O vacancy forming O adspecies that then drive CO oxidation and recover the stoichiometric Ru-doped CeO2 surface.\"\n          [5] \"The reaction mechanisms for CO oxidation and catalyst regeneration are depicted in Figure 7, consisting of three steps: (a) the oxidation of the first CO molecule on the stoichiometric Ce0.875Ru0.125O2(111) surface through participation of a lattice oxygen, leading to O vacancy formation and CO2 desorption (Figure 7a); (b) the adsorption of molecular O2 at the O vacancy, leading to the formation of surface O adspecies (Figure 7b); and (c) the interaction of a CO molecule with these O adspecies, which drives CO oxidation and regeneration of the stoichiometric Ce0.875Ru0.125O2 surface (Figure 7c).\"\n          [6] \"The reduced catalysts can be sealed by an O2 molecule from the gas phase. The adsorption energy of the O2 molecule on the O vacancy is calculated to be 1.18 eV.\"", "English": "The Mars-van Krevelen mechanism in oxide-catalyzed oxidation reactions involves the participation of lattice oxygen from the oxide surface. In this mechanism, the surface oxygen reacts with adsorbed species (e.g., CO), creating an oxygen vacancy. This vacancy is then refilled by oxygen from the gas phase, completing the catalytic cycle.\n\n          The energy required for oxygen vacancy formation (ΔEv or Ef) is crucial in determining both the catalytic activity and the oxidizing ability of the oxide surface. A lower vacancy formation energy indicates that it is easier to remove oxygen from the lattice, which generally correlates with higher catalytic activity and oxygen storage capacity (OSC).\n\n          In the case of Ru-doped CeO2 (Ce0.875Ru0.125O2), the lower Ef (1.03 eV) compared to pure CeO2 (3.20 eV) and Zr-doped CeO2 (2.03 eV) indicates higher OSC and potentially higher catalytic activity. The Ru dopant facilitates the formation of oxygen vacancies, promoting CO oxidation without an activation barrier.\n\n          The reaction mechanism for CO oxidation on Ru-doped CeO2 consists of three steps:\n          1. Oxidation of CO using lattice oxygen, forming an oxygen vacancy and CO2.\n          2. Adsorption of O2 at the oxygen vacancy, forming surface O adspecies.\n          3. Reaction of another CO molecule with these O adspecies, regenerating the oxide surface.\n\n          The significance of ΔEv lies in its ability to predict and explain the catalytic performance of oxide surfaces. Materials with lower ΔEv values are generally more active in oxidation reactions, as they can more easily provide lattice oxygen for the reaction and subsequently replenish it from the gas phase. However, an optimal ΔEv value is desired to balance high catalytic activity with catalyst stability, as extremely low values might lead to structural instability.", "Chinese": "Mars-van Krevelen机制在氧化物催化氧化反应中涉及晶格氧从氧化物表面参与反应。在这个机制中，表面氧与吸附物种（如CO）反应，产生氧空位。然后，这个空位被气相中的氧填充，完成催化循环。\n\n          氧空位形成所需的能量（ΔEv或Ef）对于确定氧化物表面的催化活性和氧化能力至关重要。较低的空位形成能表明更容易从晶格中移除氧，这通常与更高的催化活性和氧存储容量（OSC）相关。\n\n          在Ru掺杂CeO2（Ce0.875Ru0.125O2）的情况下，与纯CeO2（3.20 eV）和Zr掺杂CeO2（2.03 eV）相比，较低的Ef（1.03 eV）表明其具有更高的OSC和潜在的更高催化活性。Ru掺杂剂促进了氧空位的形成，促进了无活化能障碍的CO氧化。\n\n          Ru掺杂CeO2上CO氧化的反应机制包括三个步骤：\n          1. 使用晶格氧氧化CO，形成氧空位和CO2。\n          2. O2在氧空位处吸附，形成表面O吸附物种。\n          3. 另一个CO分子与这些O吸附物种反应，再生氧化物表面。\n\n          ΔEv的重要性在于其能够预测和解释氧化物表面的催化性能。ΔEv值较低的材料在氧化反应中通常更活跃，因为它们可以更容易地为反应提供晶格氧，并随后从气相中补充。然而，需要一个最佳的ΔEv值来平衡高催化活性和催化剂稳定性，因为过低的值可能导致结构不稳定。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp210864"},
